** NEW FILE **

IN THIS FILE, THE CLAUSES DO NOT CONTAIN THE CONSTRAINTS THAT DIFFERENT
VERSIONS OF THE SAME PACKAGE CANNOT BOTH BE INSTALLED.

The following are SAT clauses in CNF, meaning each number is a variable and
the negative numbers are the negation of that variable. (1, 2) means "1 OR 2"
and all the clauses are ANDed together.

Note that a SAT clause can also be converted to a linear inequality on boolean
variables. (x, y, z) is the same as x + y + z >= 1. For negative variables,
use NOT x = 1 - x and rearrange the constants to the RHS of the inequality (so
(x, -y, z) would be x + 1 - y + z >= 1 -> x - y + z >= 0

In addition to the clauses, the following expression should be maximized. The
eq is a tuple of coefficient variable. So [(1, 3), (2, 5)] means 1*x3 +
2*x5. Furthermore, the maximum value of the equality is easily computed and is
given as max_rhs below.

We expect in the common case that the value of the equation will be near 0.

This comes from

conda create -n test -c defaults --over --dry llvmmath anaconda

in the Python 3 version of conda.

The w dictionary maps variables to packages. pkg.rsplit('-', 2) will split a
package into name, version, build string. The build number is not strictly
included in this metadata but it should always be in the build string for
these packages. Package version comes first, then the build number.
